As a first-step\ntoward the practical\nfeasibility,\n\napplication\n\nof such devices, an investigation\n\nwith respect to performance capabilities,\n\nThis objective\n\nof\n\nwas carried out.\n\nwas achieved by studying the dynamic characteristics\n\nof somewhatidealized hopping vehicle configurations\nbased on actual conditions and mission requirements.\ndesigns were investigated.\n\nwhich are, however,\nTwo schematic\n\nOne is a single-man device assumedto be of\n\nminimumcomplexity and mass, transportable\n\nwith Apollo crews.\n\nThis\n\ndevice is intended to extend the operating range of lunar astronauts.\nThe other design is a multi-man transporter\nand duration explorations\nthe technique\n\ncapable of making long range\n\nof the lunar surface.\n\nof accelerating\n\nup a thrust-leg,\n\nmain body at the end of acceleration,\n\nBoth vehicles employ\nlocking this leg to the\n\nexecuting a classic ballistic\n\nparabola, and finally,\n\ndecelerating down this leg to complete each hop.\n\nEnergy is essentially\n\nconserved in this process, thus providing for sub-\n\nstantial\n\npayload capability,\n\nSince lunar irregularities\n\nin addition to other performance advantages.\ndo not impede hopping motion, these devices\n\ncan maintain a high average speed and visit\nfeature of interest\n\nwithin vehicle range.\niii\n\nalmost any topographic\nSpecific tasks addressed in\n\nthis\n\nstudy include investigation\n\ntransporter\n\ndesign and operation,\n\nof influencing\ndefinition\n\nfactors which affect\n\nof performance limiting\n\nphenomena,development of general operating constraints\nderivation\n\nand solution\n\nstudied, and calculation\n\nand functions3\n\nof equations of motion for each vehicle design\nof hop performance data based on digital\n\ncomputer\n\nsimulations of vehicle dynamics.\nResults of hop simulations of both transporter\nsignificant\n\nmodels indicate\n\nimprovement in performance over roving and flying\n\na\n\nvehicles.\n\nThe smaller device offers extended range to Apollo astronauts, up to\nandexceeding an operating radius of lO kin.\n\nThe larger vehicle has an\n\naverage speed of the order of 30 km/hr, very high comparedto roving unit\ndesigns.\n\nA unique hop plane changing technique used by this transporter\n\npermits these high values of average speed.
